<div id="review_2877862499" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2877862499" />
    <a title="Marianna Neal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13007653-marianna-neal"><img alt="Marianna Neal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572593566p2/13007653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2877862499?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marianna Neal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marianna Neal" href="/user/show/13007653-marianna-neal">Marianna Neal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13007653-marianna-neal?shelf=mystery-thriller-horror">mystery-thriller-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13007653-marianna-neal?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2877862499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14086507290858448932">At the time that I'm writing this the average rating for <i>The Institute</i> is 4.33 out of 5.<br/><br/>ARE. YOU. KIDDING. ME.<br/><br/>I honestly don't even know where to start here. Do I start with this book being the most derivative thing I've read in a long time? <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[It's pretty much <i>Minority Report</i> meets <i>Wanted</i>, but at a mean version of Xavier's School for Gifted Youngsters. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Do I start with the fact that almost every overdone trope you can think of in relation to the premise is present her</span>
  <span id="freeText14086507290858448932" style="display:none">At the time that I'm writing this the average rating for <i>The Institute</i> is 4.33 out of 5.<br /><br />ARE. YOU. KIDDING. ME.<br /><br />I honestly don't even know where to start here. Do I start with this book being the most derivative thing I've read in a long time? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It's pretty much <i>Minority Report</i> meets <i>Wanted</i>, but at a mean version of Xavier's School for Gifted Youngsters. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Do I start with the fact that almost every overdone trope you can think of in relation to the premise is present here? Do I mention the incredibly forced and awkward pop culture references the only purpose of which is to wave a flag that says "see?? isn't this, like, SOOO relevant?" Do I talk about these kids that sound like they're from half a century ago because no modern kid or teenager in the US actually sounds the way they do? Do I mention how difficult it was to buy a lot of the logic behind how the things at this "Institute" were done? Or that barely anything happens in the first half of this novel? Or that in a book where children are treated very cruelly King somehow managed to NOT make me care about any of these characters?<br /><br />It's all of the above, guys. It really is. For the life of me, I cannot understand how SO MANY people are loving this book, because no amount of <i>Game of Thrones</i> references can fix 561 derivative pages of disappointment. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14086507290858448932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText435843374354657214" style="display:none">I respect your review, but I disagree with it. I absolutely loved this book! I did find the ending of it dragged a little (I think it could have been cut down a little in editing), but it wasn't enough to be a big deal to me.<br /><br />I agree that many kids in the book didn't speak like real-life kids, but I must admit that if they *did* the book would have been unreadable for me, so I'm very happy with King's choice on that one! <div id="review_2989825205" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2989825205" />
    <a title="Justin Tate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23082940-justin-tate"><img alt="Justin Tate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593157920p2/23082940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2989825205?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin Tate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin Tate" href="/user/show/23082940-justin-tate">Justin Tate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2989825205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2315424893052789059">It's been 45 years since Stephen King published his first novel, Carrie, and I'm glad to say the guy's still got it. <br/><br/>The Institute thrills unevenly, taking a long time to power up, but once the wheels are in motion it's a rollercoaster ride all the way to the finish. Luke Ellis, 12-year-old brainiac, is the perfect protagonist to showcase the vulnerability and capability of kids. He's the kind of character you root for and fear for. The villains, too, are well-drawn and scary in realistic, human</span>
  <span id="freeText2315424893052789059" style="display:none">It's been 45 years since Stephen King published his first novel, Carrie, and I'm glad to say the guy's still got it. <br /><br />The Institute thrills unevenly, taking a long time to power up, but once the wheels are in motion it's a rollercoaster ride all the way to the finish. Luke Ellis, 12-year-old brainiac, is the perfect protagonist to showcase the vulnerability and capability of kids. He's the kind of character you root for and fear for. The villains, too, are well-drawn and scary in realistic, human ways. The reveal for why this Institute is locking up kids is also intriguing. You'll be glad to know it has nothing to do with giant spiders.<br /><br />Other than the slow start, the only weakness is a slightly anti-climatic finish. It's not a "bad ending" in the traditional Stephen King sense--it's actually a very satisfying conclusion--but the tension is so high going into the climax, so relentless, that the climax feels more like falling action.<br /><br />Overall, while it's unlikely fans will consider this book a Top Favorite, I would consider it a great success. Better, at least, than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2399516133?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Outsider</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1478360360?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Revival</a> because the ending actually makes sense.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2315424893052789059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2700608805" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2700608805" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2700608805?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781529355390" href="/book/show/43807359-the-institute">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2700608805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17295449404499666843">“Great events turn on small hinges.”<br/><br/>Deep in the woods of Maine, there is a facility where kids, abducted from all across America, are incarcerated.<br/><br/>Oh man, starting a new King just feels like coming home after a long day and wrapping yourself in a huge blanket... It’s hard to pinpoint exactly what it is about King’s writing that evokes such feelings, but if I could bottle it up and sell these feelings, I would, because everyone needs to experience it!<br/><br/>We all know that King does kids best. From the</span>
  <span id="freeText17295449404499666843" style="display:none">“Great events turn on small hinges.”<br /><br />Deep in the woods of Maine, there is a facility where kids, abducted from all across America, are incarcerated.<br /><br />Oh man, starting a new King just feels like coming home after a long day and wrapping yourself in a huge blanket... It’s hard to pinpoint exactly what it is about King’s writing that evokes such feelings, but if I could bottle it up and sell these feelings, I would, because everyone needs to experience it!<br /><br />We all know that King does kids best. From the Loser’s Club in IT, to the boys in The Body, he always seems to nail it! And the kids in The Institute were no exception - Avery was my personal favourite. Add in superpowers and a mysterious Institute and this has all the makings of a binge-worthy story!<br /><br />It’s a little slow at the beginning, but this is usually the case with King as he introduces the characters and the setting, before he puts his foot down and increases the pace. The parts within the Institute were my favourite, I loved getting to learn more about what was going on, whilst simultaneously worrying for those poor kids. King executes all these parts so perfectly.<br /><br />The cons, for me: it just felt a little TOO much like Firestarter in some ways. Don’t get me wrong, The Institute stands firmly as its own unique story, but I kept thinking of Firestarter similarities and it put me off slightly. Also, Tim and Wendy were two typical cookie-cutter good guys, who’s names I will undoubtedly have forgotten in a week or two. I don’t know what it is exactly, but I feel like these types of characters are more memorable in his older novels.<br /><br />Lastly, wasn’t a massive fan of the ending - it felt somewhat predictable. I’m not one who usually gets frustrated with King’s endings, but this one left me a little more on the dissatisfied side.<br /><br />That being said, I did really enjoy it overall, but unfortunately I just didn’t LOVE it. I do think it’s one of his stronger works in recent years though.<br /><br />3.75 stars - I’m introducing a new star rating for the occasion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17295449404499666843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14945681771361129589">I’m not positive why but SK does such a great job writing about kids. He seems to remember the tiniest of details; not just what scares them, but how that fear smells, tastes, and breathes down our neck. That all seems to bring the fear that we buried long ago back to the surface. <br/><br/><b>The Institute</b> was a solid 5 ⭐️ read for me.   <span id="freeText14945681771361129589" style="display:none">I’m not positive why but SK does such a great job writing about kids. He seems to remember the tiniest of details; not just what scares them, but how that fear smells, tastes, and breathes down our neck. That all seems to bring the fear that we buried long ago back to the surface. <br /><br /><b>The Institute</b> was a solid 5 ⭐️ read for me. Immediately engaged by the “night knocker” and his backstory, part of the suspense was waiting on his path to cross with our prodigy. Luke and the others in the Institute are nothing more than pawns in this horrific game to supposedly save the world from evil. Ironically by destroying the young lives of so many.<br /><br />Although this book has been compared to some of King’s older novels, I found this one much more plausible and compelling. After all, it’s the humans who are always the real monsters. As every Constant Reader can confirm...</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2988616514" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33359750-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576550045p2/33359750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2988616514?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/33359750-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43799634-the-institute">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2988616514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1539850721981493387">Ugh! I had no intention of reviewing this book, but some people can be so damned persistent! You know who you are.😤 I did kinda, sorta, but not totally love this book. Hell, truth is that the first 3/4 of it was like the Stephen King of old. It felt right. Eff that! It felt damn good! I loved the story. I loved those kids. My problem was that except in a very few instances, I wasn't too worried about them. I knew my very favorite kiddo would die. What I never really felt was the feels that Sai K</span>
  <span id="freeText1539850721981493387" style="display:none">Ugh! I had no intention of reviewing this book, but some people can be so damned persistent! You know who you are.😤 I did kinda, sorta, but not totally love this book. Hell, truth is that the first 3/4 of it was like the Stephen King of old. It felt right. Eff that! It felt damn good! I loved the story. I loved those kids. My problem was that except in a very few instances, I wasn't too worried about them. I knew my very favorite kiddo would die. What I never really felt was the feels that Sai King usually instills in every reader. King does kids like nobodies business. This time? Eh, not so much. I wanted, nay, I needed more background, or fast forward. I hated the end. It felt incomplete to me. I wanted more! I know most people say that King writes great, but his endings stink. I've NEVER found that to be the case. This time though, I'd have been happy with an extra 100 pages! By the way, no King book had ever been too long for me. Still, it was a nice feeling. Like I had missed a book from 20 years ago, and just discovered it. Wouldn't that be amazeballs? This story does have the feel of the past. I know everyone love Holly Gibney, and she and her weird shenanigans are fine. But, fuck her! I know my main man is aging and becoming tame in his golden years. Who doesn't? Still, I would like my favorite author to scare the shit outta me before I die! Whatever. The book is good. Didn't blow my mind though. Still, it beats Gerald's Game, and Delores Claiborne! <br />Sorry guys, I may be a wee bit grumpy lately!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14793382902060849717"><b>
  <i>The Institute</i>
</b> has easily become my favorite Stephen King novel, <i>ever!</i> It may be over 500 pages, but this book reads so fast, you won't put it down. I would say that this book is a combination of X-Men meets Stranger Things—with the literary horror writing style that you've expected to love by Stephen King. The characters were multifaceted, the story was gripping and original, and there wasn't too much exposition—we got right into the story early on. This story really will take you on an adve</span>
  <span id="freeText14793382902060849717" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>The Institute</i>
</b> has easily become my favorite Stephen King novel, <i>ever!</i> It may be over 500 pages, but this book reads so fast, you won't put it down. I would say that this book is a combination of X-Men meets Stranger Things—with the literary horror writing style that you've expected to love by Stephen King. The characters were multifaceted, the story was gripping and original, and there wasn't too much exposition—we got right into the story early on. This story really will take you on an adventure that you weren't expecting, and you will definitely not expect how it turns out. <b>
  <i>The Institute</i>
</b> will get you thinking and I see big things for this release. </span>

Although I will say, I wouldn’t class this as horror - considering it won the a Goodreads choice award for horror, for me this was firmly in the thriller genre. But I loved it nonetheless! <br/><br/>We start with Tim Jamieson, an ex cop flying from Florida to NYC. When someone is required to give up their seat Tim volunteers and decides to hitch hike.   <span id="freeText4379254072811192245" style="display:none"><i> “Hell is waiting, I’ll be here to meet you.” </i> <br /><br />4 stars ⭐️ <br /><br />This was an absolute ride! Although I will say, I wouldn’t class this as horror - considering it won the a Goodreads choice award for horror, for me this was firmly in the thriller genre. But I loved it nonetheless! <br /><br />We start with Tim Jamieson, an ex cop flying from Florida to NYC. When someone is required to give up their seat Tim volunteers and decides to hitch hike. He makes it to DuPray North Carolina, where he takes a night knocker job for the local Sheriff. <br /><br />Just as we get settled in with Tim though, the scene changes to 12 year old Luke Ellis. A boy of extremely high intelligence, who wakes up one morning to find he has been kidnapped and taken to The Institute, a place of violence and fear. <br /><br />As the book continues we find out more about The Institute and it’s purpose. I will admit a fair bit went over my head - I’m not one for conspiracies or psychic abilities but the action filled plot kept me reading. I wanted to see what would happen. <br /><br />I was saddened by how some of it played out, but overall it was a thrill ride and I would recommend. Also Orphan Annie is the BEST character 😊<br /><br />******************<br /><br />In my attempt to read more Stephen King I’ve checked this one out from the library 😊</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2698737343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4781365927492540259"><b>The five star beginning</b> takes place on a totally booked Delta flight bound for New York where we meet Tim Jamieson who gives up his seat and ends up with a job as a Night Knocker in a small backward rural town, population 5,400.<p> There we learn more about Tim's eventful previous life and meet some crazy good <b>people of the night</b>....like homeless Orphan Annie, my favorite.</p><p> As SK states in his author notes, <b>THE INSTITUTE</b> is mostly about kids, and with a group of exceptionally gifted kidnapped childr</p></span>
  <span id="freeText4781365927492540259" style="display:none"><b>The five star beginning</b> takes place on a totally booked Delta flight bound for New York where we meet Tim Jamieson who gives up his seat and ends up with a job as a Night Knocker in a small backward rural town, population 5,400.<p> There we learn more about Tim's eventful previous life and meet some crazy good <b>people of the night</b>....like homeless Orphan Annie, my favorite.</p><p> As SK states in his author notes, <b>THE INSTITUTE</b> is mostly about kids, and with a group of exceptionally gifted kidnapped children is where we spend most of our reading time as we leave southern Carolina for the secretive, deadly compound hidden deep in the woods of northern Maine.</p><p> As the brilliant 12 year old Luke Ellis awakens in a similar, but unknown environment, he soon discovers a scary, threatening new life of horror among other draftees like himself....escape his only hope of survival.</p><p>Another winner for <b>KING</b> but instead of horror, a mystery-thriller with lots of evil characters and some psychic phenomena. As always, <b>KING</b> brings back memories of old....remember candy cigarettes (yum!), "prehistoric" (lol) sitcoms like Bewitched and Happy Days, and once again, he also gets in some personal political digs about current republican leadership. The only reference to his other novels I picked up was mention of "twins of an old horror movie” (The Shining) and The Outsider(s).</p><p> <b> GREAT</b> story - <b>GREAT</b> characters - <b>GREAT</b> read, but personally I wanted more of Tim Jamieson and the <b>people of the night!</b></p></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2797318637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3637776804897061338">Video review (will be live at 5am CST): <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/F6ur3r67dkc'>https://youtu.be/F6ur3r67dkc</a><br/><br/>After the thinly-veiled-political-stance-marketed-as-a-novella that was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38355410.Elevation' title='Elevation by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elevation</a>, Stephen King returns to form with his most thought-provoking book since <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20926278.Revival' title='Revival by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Revival</a>. You're going to see loads of people, Trumpkins and anti-Trumpers alike, complaining or cheering over FIVE. FUCKING. SENTENCES. in a 560 page book. It truly is as ridiculous as it sounds, and that's coming from a guy (*waves* talking about me) who lost his fucking mind</span>
  <span id="freeText3637776804897061338" style="display:none">Video review (will be live at 5am CST): <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/F6ur3r67dkc">https://youtu.be/F6ur3r67dkc</a><br /><br />After the thinly-veiled-political-stance-marketed-as-a-novella that was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38355410.Elevation" title="Elevation by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Elevation</a>, Stephen King returns to form with his most thought-provoking book since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20926278.Revival" title="Revival by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Revival</a>. You're going to see loads of people, Trumpkins and anti-Trumpers alike, complaining or cheering over FIVE. FUCKING. SENTENCES. in a 560 page book. It truly is as ridiculous as it sounds, and that's coming from a guy (*waves* talking about me) who lost his fucking mind when the Orange One took office. I admittedly went a bit crazy but I dug myself out and here we are. The aforementioned five sentences don't follow each other. Some are even hundreds of pages apart. There's even a GOOD GUY with a picture of Trump on his wall, but you won't hear anyone talking about that. The Trump stuff isn't any more invasive than all the times King has ragged on Nixon, Clinton, and Bush over the years, so calm yo chest meat, Bartholomew, and stop flinching at shadows. <br /><br />If you're a horror fan who thinks King lost his way once he stopped writing about undead pets and vampires, you should probably skip this one. King has matured once again, and while the book is scary in an intelligent way, it is NOT. A. HORROR. NOVEL. <b>Hard stop.</b> It's not like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/830502.It" title="It by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">It</a>, so don't listen to the marketing. It is, however, a novel about kids, human monsters, and the lengths some people will go to to ensure the survival of the human race based solely on what MIGHT happen and not what WILL happen. <br /><br />You do not need to have read any of King's previous books to get this one, but it would behoove you to have read any of his stuff that focuses on psychic powers. The Shop, from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233667.Firestarter" title="Firestarter by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Firestarter</a> and other works, makes no appearance here. Not in name, anyway. Can it be assumed that's who's behind the titular Institute? Mayhap it can. But I repeat, you need no knowledge of any previously-published King books. However, if you are in possession of this knowledge, you're going to have a much deeper experience.<br /><br />Still with me? Cool. All of the above are responses to questions I've been asked since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43798285.The_Institute" title="The Institute by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Institute</a> came out. Now we can get into my personal feelings about this book.<br /><br />I had a motherfucking blast. I took my time and whittled away at this one over the course of a week, about 75 pages a day, and I highly recommend you do the same. You will be tempted to speed through because this does feel like a thriller but I assure you that's just the paint job. This thing is built on a literary chassis, and has a monster of a theme under its hood. In other words, she fires on all cylinders, sports fans, so buckle up and enjoy the ride. If you do choose to race rather than take a leisurely drive, I can dig it. I almost had the same problem. These are just suggestions. You do you, Becky. Moving on.<br /><br />This is, hands down, legs spread, tits to the sky, one of King's best endings. I was clapping during the final showdown and vibrating with excitement. I'm still ruminating on this next statement but... I might just call it King's BEST ending. If there are plot holes, I'll leave those for Kemper and Dan 2.0 to find because I didn't notice any. What I'm saying is:<br /><br />This is disbelief...<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />...and this is me. Needless to say, it was adequately suspended. <br /><br />In summation: HOLY SHIT I LOVED THIS FUCKING BOOK. Don't @ me if you didn't like it, Beatrice, and if you're one of these clowns on either side stuck on stupid over five sentences, can I possibly direct you to a good therapist? Worked wonders for me. <br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: How they gonna do the Lot like that???</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3637776804897061338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2938503927" />
    <a title="Ginger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger"><img alt="Ginger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593449448p2/14097149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2938503927?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ginger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ginger" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger">Ginger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2938503927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5516885951098437725"><b>5 STARS!!!</b><br/><br/>Uncle Steve's still got it! I know the hype train has been hot for this one but I kept myself in check. <br/><br/>...but it's warranted folks.<br/><br/><b>The Institute</b> was a fast paced thriller from the beginning to the end and I really loved this one. The characters were fantastic, the writing was great and the whole plot was well thought out.<br/><br/><b>The Institute</b> starts off with introducing us to Tim Jamieson. I wasn't quite sure where this character's arc was going to go in the beginning, but I'm glad I kept rea</span>
  <span id="freeText5516885951098437725" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS!!!</b><br /><br />Uncle Steve's still got it! I know the hype train has been hot for this one but I kept myself in check. <br /><br />...but it's warranted folks.<br /><br /><b>The Institute</b> was a fast paced thriller from the beginning to the end and I really loved this one. The characters were fantastic, the writing was great and the whole plot was well thought out.<br /><br /><b>The Institute</b> starts off with introducing us to Tim Jamieson. I wasn't quite sure where this character's arc was going to go in the beginning, but I'm glad I kept reading.<br />Because <i>Stephen King</i> has a plan with this character and I loved everything about Tim!<br /><br />After following Tim's journey for a bit, we're introduced to Luke Ellis.<br /><br />Gosh, I love Luke! He's such a great character. I loved all of the kids that are at the Institute and I felt so bad for them. <br />From Sha's positivity, Nicky's rebellion to Avery's sweetness. Each kid had their own voice and I felt <i>King</i> did a great job writing each one of them.<br /><br />I hated everyone that was part of this program and the role that they played. You could tell that their fanatical and uncompromising pursuit of the agenda was in full effect.<br /><br />The ending was <b>NOT</b> a disappointment!<br />I've suffered with other books by <i>King</i> in where the ending fizzled out but that's not the case in <b>The Institute</b>. The pacing was fast and I just kept flipping the pages. I had to find out what would happen to Luke, all the kids and what Tim's role would be on taking out the Institute.<br /><br />I'm really glad I read this one and I hope <i>King</i> keeps rolling books out like this. It's definitely worth they hype!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5516885951098437725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tlWKHJM5UDPQahx6vlNXZ0OM1rzvRGqmk+7kjvwl17CiZrWOJdJI3QNwWjzlNm7ntt8j7sYpPd7EG7Dgbo8xwg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13389483338033288062">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText13389483338033288062" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13389483338033288062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
